href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight saving time">DST</a>)</span></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/UTC%2B02:00" title="UTC+02:00">UTC+02:00</a> (<a href="/wiki/Central_European_Summer_Time" title="Central European Summer Time">CEST</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/List_of_postal_codes_in_Germany" title="List of postal codes in Germany">Postal codes</a></th><td class="infobox-data adr"><div class="postal-code">55116\xe2\x80\x9355131</div></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/List_of_dialling_codes_in_Germany" title="List of dialling codes in Germany">Dialling codes</a></th><td class="infobox-data">06131, 06136</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><a href="/wiki/Vehicle_registration_plate" title="Vehicle rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.mainz.de/">www.mainz.de</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg/220px-Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg/330px-Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg/440px-Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="958" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sattelite_Wiesbaden_Mainz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satellite view of Mainz (south of the Rhine) and Wiesbaden</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Mainz</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/a\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;tide&#39;">a\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <small>German:&#32;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ma\xc9\xaa\xcc\xafnt\xcd\xa1s]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:De-Mainz.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5d/De-Mainz.ogg" class="internal" title="De-Mainz.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la">Mogontiacum</i>) is the capital and largest city of <a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>. \n</p><p>Most of the city is upstream of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> before it flows west. The north of the city faces <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden" title="Wiesbaden">Wiesbaden</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a>, and the east the <a href="/wiki/Confluence" title="Confluence">confluence</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Main_(river)" title="Main (river)">Main</a>. \n</p><p>Mainz is an <a href="/wiki/Independent_city" title="Independent city">independent city</a> with a population of 218,578 (as of 2019) and forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Rhine-Main" title="Frankfurt Rhine-Main">Frankfurt Rhine-Main Metropolitan Region</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Mainz was founded by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a> in the 1st century BC as a military fortress on the northernmost frontier of the empire and provincial capital of <a href="/wiki/Germania_Superior" title="Germania Superior">Germania Superior</a>. Mainz became an important city in the 8th century AD as part of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, capital of the <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Mainz" title="Electorate of Mainz">Electorate of Mainz</a> and seat of the <a href="/wiki/Elector_of_Mainz" title="Elector of Mainz">Archbishop-Elector of Mainz</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Primate_(bishop)" title="Primate (bishop)">Primate</a> of Germany. Mainz is famous as the home of <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Gutenberg" title="Johannes Gutenberg">Johannes Gutenberg</a>, the inventor of the movable-type <a href="/wiki/Printing_press" title="Printing press">printing press</a>, who in the early 1450s manufactured his first books in the city, including the <a href="/wiki/Gutenberg_Bible" title="Gutenberg Bible">Gutenberg Bible</a>. Mainz was heavily damaged in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>; more than <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Mainz_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Mainz in World War II">30 air raids</a> destroyed most of the historic buildings. \n</p><p>Mainz is notable as a <a href="/wiki/Transport_hub" title="Transport hub">transport hub</a>, for <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a> production, and for its many rebuilt historic buildings.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label cities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#Alternative_names"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Alternative names</span></a></li>\n<li class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Topography">Topography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Topography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Mainz is on the 50th latitude north, on the <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">left bank of the Rhine</a>. The east of the city is opposite where the <a href="/wiki/Main_(river)" title="Main (river)">Main</a> falls into it. The population in the early 2012 was 200,957. An further 18,619 people live mainly elsewhere but have a <a href="/wiki/Vacation_property" class="mw-redirect" title="Vacation property">second home</a> in Mainz. The city is part of the Rhein Metro area of 5.8 million people. Mainz can easily be reached from <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt International Airport">Frankfurt International Airport</a> in 25 minutes by commuter railway <a href="/wiki/S8_(Rhine-Main_S-Bahn)" title="S8 (Rhine-Main S-Bahn)">Line S8</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainz_aerial_photograph.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Mainz_aerial_photograph.jpg/500px-Mainz_aerial_photograph.jpg" decoding="async" width="500" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Mainz_aerial_photograph.jpg/750px-Mainz_aerial_photograph.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Mainz_aerial_photograph.jpg/1000px-Mainz_aerial_photograph.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainz_aerial_photograph.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View north along the Rhine with the old Winterhafen in the lower left and the former port facilities further north</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:50._Breitengrad_in_Mainz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/50._Breitengrad_in_Mainz.jpg/150px-50._Breitengrad_in_Mainz.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/50._Breitengrad_in_Mainz.jpg/225px-50._Breitengrad_in_Mainz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/50._Breitengrad_in_Mainz.jpg/300px-50._Breitengrad_in_Mainz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:50._Breitengrad_in_Mainz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>50th Latitude on the Gutenbergplatz</div></div></div>\n<p>Mainz is a <a href="/wiki/River_port" class="mw-redirect" title="River port">river port</a> city as the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> which connects with its main tributaries, such as the <a href="/wiki/Neckar" title="Neckar">Neckar</a>, the Main and, later, the <a href="/wiki/Moselle_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Moselle (river)">Moselle</a> and thereby continental Europe with the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rotterdam" title="Port of Rotterdam">Port of Rotterdam</a> and thus the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>. Mainz\'s history and economy are closely tied to its proximity to the Rhine historically handling much of the region\'s waterborne cargo. Today\'s huge <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Mainz" title="Port of Mainz">container port hub</a> allowing <a href="/wiki/Multimodal_transport" title="Multimodal transport">trimodal transport</a> is north of the town centre. The <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">river moderates climate</a>. It makes waterfront neighborhoods slightly warmer in winter and cooler in summer.\n</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Quaternary_glaciation" title="Quaternary glaciation">last ice age</a>, sand dunes were deposited in the Rhine valley at what was to become the western edge of the city. The <a href="/wiki/Mainz_Sand_Dunes" title="Mainz Sand Dunes">Mainz Sand Dunes</a> area is now a nature reserve with a unique landscape and rare <i>steppe</i> vegetation for this area.\n</p><p>While the Mainz legion camp was founded in 13/12 BC on the K\xc3\xa4strich hill, the associated <a href="/wiki/Vicus" title="Vicus">vici</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canabae" class="mw-redirect" title="Canabae">canabae</a> (civilian settlements) were erected towards the Rhine. Historical sources and archaeological findings both prove the importance of the military and civilian Mogontiacum as a port city on the Rhine.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Mainz experiences an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification</a> <i>Cfb</i>).\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible" style="width:100%; text-align:center; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="14">Climate style="background: #BABAFF; color:#000000;">46<br />(1.8)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #B9B9FF; color:#000000; border-left-width:medium">550<br />(21.5)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source: <i>Intellicast</i><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Mainz" title="Timeline of Mainz">Timeline of Mainz</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Mogontiacum">Roman Mogontiacum</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Roman Mogontiacum">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadttor1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Stadttor1.jpg/220px-Stadttor1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Stadttor1.jpg/330px-Stadttor1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Stadttor1.jpg/440px-Stadttor1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadttor1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Remains of a Roman town gate from the late 4th century</div></div></div>\n<p>The Roman stronghold or <i><a href="/wiki/Castrum" class="mw-redirect" title="Castrum">castrum</a> <b>Mogontiacum</b></i>, the precursor to Mainz, was founded by the Roman general <a href="/wiki/Nero_Claudius_Drusus" title="Nero Claudius Drusus">Drusus</a> perhaps as early as 13/12 BC. As related by <a href="/wiki/Suetonius" title="Suetonius">Suetonius</a> the existence of <i>Mogontiacum</i> is well established by four years later (the account of the death and funeral of <a href="/wiki/Nero_Claudius_Drusus" title="Nero Claudius Drusus">Nero Claudius Drusus</a>), though several other theories suggest the site may have been established earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Although the city is situated opposite the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Main_(river)" title="Main (river)">Main</a>, the name of Mainz is not from <i>Main</i>, the similarity being perhaps reinforced by <a href="/wiki/Folk_etymology" title="Folk etymology">folk-etymological</a> reanalysis. <i>Main</i> is from Latin <i>Moenis</i> (also <i>Moenus</i> or <i>Menus</i>), the name the Romans used for the river. <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">Linguistic</a> analysis of the many forms that the name "Mainz" has taken on make it clear that it is a simplification of <i>Mogontiacum</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The name appears to be <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">Celtic</a> and ultimately it is. However, it had also become Roman and was selected by them with a special significance. The Roman soldiers defending <a href="/wiki/Gallia" class="mw-redirect" title="Gallia">Gallia</a> had adopted the Gallic god <a href="/wiki/Mogons" title="Mogons">Mogons</a> (Mogounus, Moguns, Mogonino), for the meaning of which etymology offers two basic options: "the great one", similar to Latin magnus, which was used in aggrandizing names such as <i>Alexander magnus</i>, "Alexander the Great" and <i>Pompeius magnus</i>, "Pompey the great", or the god of "might" personified as it appears in young servitors of any type whether of noble or ignoble birth.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zitadelle_Mainz_Drususstein.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Zitadelle_Mainz_Drususstein.jpg/170px-Zitadelle_Mainz_Drususstein.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Zitadelle_Mainz_Drususstein.jpg/255px-Zitadelle_Mainz_Drususstein.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Zitadelle_Mainz_Drususstein.jpg/340px-Zitadelle_Mainz_Drususstein.jpg 2x" data-file-width="667" data-file-height="1001" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zitadelle_Mainz_Drususstein.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Drusus monument or <a href="/wiki/Drususstein" title="Drususstein">Drususstein</a> (surrounded by the 17th century citadel) raised by Drusus\' men to commemorate him</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mz-roemer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Mz-roemer.jpg/220px-Mz-roemer.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Mz-roemer.jpg/330px-Mz-roemer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Mz-roemer.jpg/440px-Mz-roemer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mz-roemer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Remains of the Roman aqueduct</div></div></div>\n<p>Mogontiacum was an important military town throughout Roman times, probably due to its strategic position at the confluence of the Main and the Rhine. The town of <i>Mogontiacum</i> grew up between the fort and the river. The castrum was the base of <a href="/wiki/Legio_XIV_Gemina" title="Legio XIV Gemina">Legio XIV <i>Gemina</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/Legio_XVI_Gallica" title="Legio XVI Gallica">XVI <i>Gallica</i></a> (AD 9\xe2\x80\x9343), <a href="/wiki/Legio_XXII_Primigenia" title="Legio XXII Primigenia">XXII <i>Primigenia</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Legio_IV_Macedonica" title="Legio IV Macedonica">IV <i>Macedonica</i></a> (43\xe2\x80\x9370), <a href="/wiki/Legio_I_Adiutrix" title="Legio I Adiutrix">I <i>Adiutrix</i></a> (70\xe2\x80\x9388), <a href="/wiki/Legio_XXI_Rapax" title="Legio XXI Rapax">XXI <i>Rapax</i></a> (70\xe2\x80\x9389), and <a href="/wiki/Legio_XIV_Gemina" title="Legio XIV Gemina">XIV <i>Gemina</i></a> (70\xe2\x80\x9392), among others. Mainz was also a base of a Roman river fleet, the <a href="/wiki/Classis_Germanica" title="Classis Germanica">Classis Germanica</a>. Remains of Roman troop ships (<a href="/wiki/Navis_lusoria" title="Navis lusoria">navis lusoria</a>) and a patrol boat from the late 4th century were discovered in 1982/86 and may now be viewed in the <i>Museum f\xc3\xbcr Antike Schifffahrt</i>. A temple dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Isis" title="Isis">Isis Panthea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cybele" title="Cybele">Magna Mater</a> was discovered in 2000<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> and is open to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The city was the provincial capital of <a href="/wiki/Germania_Superior" title="Germania Superior">Germania Superior</a>, and had an important funeral monument dedicated to Drusus, to which people made pilgrimages for an annual festival from as far away as <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a>. Among the famous buildings were the largest <a href="/wiki/Roman_Theatre_(Mainz)" title="Roman Theatre (Mainz)">theatre</a> north of the Alps and a bridge across the Rhine. The city was also the site of the assassination of emperor <a href="/wiki/Severus_Alexander" title="Severus Alexander">Severus Alexander</a> in 235.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Alemanni" title="Alemanni">Alemanni</a> forces under <a href="/wiki/Rando_(king)" title="Rando (king)">Rando</a> sacked the city in 368. From the last day of 405<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> or 406, the Siling and Asding <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alans</a>, and other Germanic tribes <a href="/wiki/Crossing_of_the_Rhine" title="Crossing of the Rhine">crossed the Rhine</a>, possibly at Mainz. Christian chronicles relate that the bishop, Aureus, was put to death by the Alemannian Crocus. The way was open to the sack of <a href="/wiki/Trier" title="Trier">Trier</a> and the invasion of Gaul.\n</p><p>Throughout the changes of time, the Roman castrum never seems to have been permanently abandoned as a military installation, which is a testimony to Roman military judgement. Different structures were built there at different times. The current citadel originated in 1660, but it replaced previous forts. It was used in World War II. One of the sights at the citadel is still the <a href="/wiki/Cenotaph" title="Cenotaph">cenotaph</a> raised by legionaries to commemorate their <a href="/wiki/Nero_Claudius_Drusus_Germanicus" class="mw-redirect" title="Nero Claudius Drusus Germanicus">Drusus</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Frankish_Mainz">Frankish Mainz</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Frankish Mainz">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-top-width:0;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><caption style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2018</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">217,118</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+8.4%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">source:<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Wikipedia_and_sources_that_mirror_or_use_it" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="This claim cites another Wikipedia article. Articles need references to reliable third-party sources. (May 2020)">circular reference</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Through a series of incursions during the 4th century <a href="/wiki/Alsace" title="Alsace">Alsace</a> gradually lost its Belgic ethnic character of formerly Germanic tribes among Celts ruled by Romans and became predominantly influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Alamanni" class="mw-redirect" title="Alamanni">Alamanni</a>. The Romans repeatedly re-asserted control; however, the troops stationed at Mainz became chiefly non-Italic and the emperors had only one or two Italian ancestors in a pedigree that included chiefly peoples of the northern frontier.\n</p><p>The last emperor to station troops serving the western empire at Mainz was <a href="/wiki/Valentinian_III" title="Valentinian III">Valentinian III</a> (reigned 425\xe2\x80\x93455), who relied heavily on his <i>Magister militum per Gallias</i>, <a href="/wiki/Flavius_A%C3%ABtius" class="mw-redirect" title="Flavius A\xc3\xabtius">Flavius A\xc3\xabtius</a>. By that time the army included large numbers of troops from the major Germanic confederacies along the Rhine, the Alamanni, the <a href="/wiki/Saxons" title="Saxons">Saxons</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a>. The Franks were an opponent that had risen to power and reputation among the Belgae of the lower Rhine during the 3rd century and repeatedly attempted to extend their influence upstream. In 358 the emperor <a href="/wiki/Julian_the_Apostate" class="mw-redirect" title="Julian the Apostate">Julian</a> bought peace by giving them most of <a href="/wiki/Germania_Inferior" title="Germania Inferior">Germania Inferior</a>, which they possessed anyway, and imposing service in the Roman army in exchange.\n</p><p>European factions in the time of master A\xc3\xabtius included Celts, Goths, Franks, Saxons, Alamanni, Huns, Italians, and Alans as well as numerous other minor peoples. A\xc3\xabtius played them all off against one another in a masterly effort to keep the peace under Roman sovereignty. He used Hunnic troops a number of times. At last a day of reckoning arrived between A\xc3\xabtius and <a href="/wiki/Attila" title="Attila">Attila</a>, both commanding polyglot, multi-ethnic troops. Attila went through Alsace in 451, devastating the country and destroying Mainz and Trier with their Roman garrisons. Shortly after he was thwarted by <a href="/wiki/Flavius_A%C3%ABtius" class="mw-redirect" title="Flavius A\xc3\xabtius">Flavius A\xc3\xabtius</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ch%C3%A2lons" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Ch\xc3\xa2lons">Battle of Ch\xc3\xa2lons</a>, the largest of the ancient world.\n</p><p>A\xc3\xabtius was not to enjoy the victory long. He was assassinated in 454 by the hand of his employer, who in turn was stabbed to death by friends of A\xc3\xabtius in 455. As far as the north was concerned this was the effective end of the Roman empire there. After some sanguinary but relatively brief contention a former subordinate of A\xc3\xabtius, <a href="/wiki/Ricimer" title="Ricimer">Ricimer</a>, became commander in chief, and was named Patrician. His father was a Suebian; his mother, a princess of the <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a>. Ricimer did not rule the north directly but set up a client province there, which functioned independently. The capital was at <a href="/wiki/Soissons" title="Soissons">Soissons</a>. Even then its status was equivocal. Many insisted it was the <a href="/wiki/Domain_of_Soissons" class="mw-redirect" title="Domain of Soissons">Kingdom of Soissons</a>. which extended across northern France and was ruled in the name of Rome by Aegidius, an ally of emperor Majorian, 457\xe2\x80\x93461, who died about 464. He was succeeded by his son, Syagrius, who was defeated by Clovis in 486.\n</p><p>Previously the first of the <a href="/wiki/Merovingian" class="mw-redirect" title="Merovingian">Merovingians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clodio" class="mw-redirect" title="Clodio">Clodio</a>, had been defeated by A\xc3\xabtius at about 430. His son, <a href="/wiki/Merovaeus" class="mw-redirect" title="Merovaeus">Merovaeus</a>, fought on the Roman side against Attila, and his son, <a href="/wiki/Childeric_I" title="Childeric I">Childeric</a>, served in the domain of Soissons. Meanwhile, the Franks were gradually infiltrating and assuming power in this domain from Txxandria (northern Belgium which had been given to them by the Romans to protect as allies). They also moved up the Rhine and created a domain in the region of the former Germania Superior with capital at <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>. They became known as the <a href="/wiki/Ripuarian_Franks" title="Ripuarian Franks">Ripuarian Franks</a> as opposed to the <a href="/wiki/Salian_Franks" title="Salian Franks">Salian Franks</a>. Events moved rapidly in the late 5th century.\n</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Western Roman Empire">fall of the Western Roman Empire</a> in 476, the <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a> under the rule of <a href="/wiki/Clovis_I" title="Clovis I">Clovis I</a> gained control over western Europe by the year 496. Clovis, son of Childeric, became king of the Salians in 481, ruling from <a href="/wiki/Tournai" title="Tournai">Tournai</a>. In 486 he defeated <a href="/wiki/Syagrius" title="Syagrius">Syagrius</a>, last governor of the Soissons domain, and took northern France. He extended his reign to <a href="/wiki/Cambrai" title="Cambrai">Cambrai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tongeren" title="Tongeren">Tongeren</a> in 490\xe2\x80\x93491, and repelled the Alamanni in 496. Also in that year he converted to Catholicism from non-<a href="/wiki/Arian_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Arian Christianity">Arian Christianity</a>. Clovis annexed the kingdom of Cologne in 508. Thereafter, Mainz, in its strategic position, became one of the bases of the Frankish kingdom. Mainz had sheltered a Christian community long before the conversion of Clovis. His successor <a href="/wiki/Dagobert_I" title="Dagobert I">Dagobert I</a> reinforced the walls of Mainz and made it one of his seats. A <a href="/wiki/Solidus_(coin)" title="Solidus (coin)">solidus</a> of <a href="/wiki/Theodebert_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Theodebert I">Theodebert I</a> (534\xe2\x80\x93548) was minted at Mainz.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> (768\xe2\x80\x93814), through a succession of wars against other tribes, built a vast Frankian empire in Europe. Mainz from its central location became important to the empire and to Christianity. Meanwhile, language change was gradually working to divide the Franks. Mainz spoke a dialect termed <a href="/wiki/Ripuarian_language" title="Ripuarian language">Ripuarian</a>. On the death of Charlemagne, distinctions between France and Germany began to be made. Mainz was not central any longer but was on the border, creating a question of the nationality to which it belonged, which descended into modern times as the question of Alsace-Lorraine.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christian_Mainz">Christian Mainz</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Christian Mainz">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="infobox geography vcard" style="font-size:88%;"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above adr" style="padding:0.25em 0.33em 0.33em;line-height:1.2em;font-size:1.25em;"><div style="display:inline" class="fn org country-name">Free City of Mainz</div><br /><div style="padding-top:0.25em; font-weight:normal;"><i>Freie Stadt Mainz</i></div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-subheader">1244\xe2\x80\x931462</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Status</th><td class="infobox-data">Imperial city</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Capital</th><td class="infobox-data">Mainz</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Government</th><td class="infobox-data">Imperial city</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Historical era</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">\xe2\x80\xa2&#160;City established </div></th><td class="infobox-data">c. 13 BC</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">\xe2\x80\xa2&#160;<a href="/wiki/German_town_law" title="German town law">City charter</a> granted<br /><span class="nowrap">&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>by <a href="/wiki/Siegfried_III_(Archbishop_of_Mainz)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siegfried III (Archbishop of Mainz)">Abp Siegfried III</a> </div></th><td class="infobox-data">1244</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">\xe2\x80\xa2&#160;Rival archbishops title="Adolph II of Nassau">Abp Adolph II</a> </div></th><td class="infobox-data">1462</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><div colspan="2">\n</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data">\n<table style="width:95%; background: transparent; text-align:center; margin:0 auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="vertical-align:top; text-align:center;border:0;">\n<table style="width:92%; background:transparent; text-align:center; margin:0 auto; border:0;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="border:0; padding:0; part of</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" decoding="async" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Mainz" title="Electorate of Mainz">Electorate of Mainz</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainzer_Dom_vom_Kreuzgang.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Mainzer_Dom_vom_Kreuzgang.jpg/170px-Mainzer_Dom_vom_Kreuzgang.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Mainzer_Dom_vom_Kreuzgang.jpg/255px-Mainzer_Dom_vom_Kreuzgang.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Mainzer_Dom_vom_Kreuzgang.jpg/340px-Mainzer_Dom_vom_Kreuzgang.jpg 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainzer_Dom_vom_Kreuzgang.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mainz_Cathedral" title="Mainz Cathedral">Mainz Cathedral</a>, western main tower</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Stephan_zu_Mainz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/St_Stephan_zu_Mainz.jpg/170px-St_Stephan_zu_Mainz.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/St_Stephan_zu_Mainz.jpg/255px-St_Stephan_zu_Mainz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/St_Stephan_zu_Mainz.jpg/340px-St_Stephan_zu_Mainz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="675" data-file-height="900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Stephan_zu_Mainz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St._Stephan_Mainz" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Stephan Mainz">St. Stephan Mainz</a> (St. Stephan Church in Mainz) is famous for its <a href="/wiki/Marc_Chagall" title="Marc Chagall">Marc Chagall</a> windows</div></div></div>\n<p>In the early <a href="/wiki/Middle_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle Age">Middle Ages</a>, Mainz was a centre for the <a href="/wiki/Christianization" title="Christianization">Christianisation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slavic_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Slavic peoples">Slavic peoples</a>. The first archbishop in Mainz, <a href="/wiki/Boniface" class="mw-redirect" title="Boniface">Boniface</a>, was killed in 754 while trying to convert the <a href="/wiki/Frisians" title="Frisians">Frisians</a> to Christianity and is buried in <a href="/wiki/Fulda" title="Fulda">Fulda</a>. Boniface held a personal title of archbishop; Mainz became a regular archbishopric see in 781, when Boniface\'s successor <a href="/wiki/Lullus" title="Lullus">Lullus</a> was granted the <a href="/wiki/Pallium" title="Pallium">pallium</a> by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Adrian_I" title="Pope Adrian I">Pope Adrian I</a>. <a href="/wiki/Harald_Klak" title="Harald Klak">Harald Klak</a>, king of Jutland, his family and followers, were baptized at Mainz in 826, in the <a href="/wiki/St._Alban%27s_Abbey,_Mainz" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Alban&#39;s Abbey, Mainz">abbey of St. Alban\'s</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>  Other early archbishops of Mainz include <a href="/wiki/Rabanus_Maurus" title="Rabanus Maurus">Rabanus Maurus</a>, the scholar and author, and <a href="/wiki/Willigis" title="Willigis">Willigis</a> (975\xe2\x80\x931011), who began construction on the current building of the <a href="/wiki/Mainz_Cathedral" title="Mainz Cathedral">Mainz Cathedral</a> and founded the monastery of St. Stephan.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bonifazius.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bonifazius.jpg/170px-Bonifazius.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bonifazius.jpg/255px-Bonifazius.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bonifazius.jpg/340px-Bonifazius.jpg 2x" data-file-width="683" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bonifazius.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Monument to <a href="/wiki/St._Boniface" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Boniface">St. Boniface</a> before Mainz Cathedral</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wenzel_Hollar_Mainzer_Dom_1632.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Wenzel_Hollar_Mainzer_Dom_1632.jpg/220px-Wenzel_Hollar_Mainzer_Dom_1632.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Wenzel_Hollar_Mainzer_Dom_1632.jpg/330px-Wenzel_Hollar_Mainzer_Dom_1632.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Wenzel_Hollar_Mainzer_Dom_1632.jpg/440px-Wenzel_Hollar_Mainzer_Dom_1632.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="419" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wenzel_Hollar_Mainzer_Dom_1632.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>St. Martin\'s Cathedral in Mainz, by <a href="/wiki/Wenzel_Hollar" class="mw-redirect" title="Wenzel Hollar">Wenzel Hollar</a>; pen-and-ink drawing 1632</div></div></div>\n<p>From the time of Willigis until the end of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> in 1806, the <a href="/wiki/Archbishops_of_Mainz" class="mw-redirect" title="Archbishops of Mainz">Archbishops of Mainz</a> were archchancellors of the Empire and the most important of the seven <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">Electors</a> of the German emperor. Besides Rome, the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Mainz" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Mainz">diocese of Mainz</a> today is the only <a href="/wiki/Diocese" title="Diocese">diocese</a> in the world with an <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_see" title="Episcopal see">episcopal see</a> that is called a <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> (<i>sancta sedes</i>). The Archbishops of Mainz traditionally were <i><a href="/wiki/Primas_germaniae" class="mw-redirect" title="Primas germaniae">primas germaniae</a></i>, the substitutes of the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Pope</a> north of the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>.\n</p><p>In 1244, Archbishop <a href="/wiki/Siegfried_III_(archbishop_of_Mainz)" title="Siegfried III (archbishop of Mainz)">Siegfried III</a> granted Mainz a city charter, which included the right of the citizens to establish and elect a city council. The city saw a feud between two archbishops in 1461, namely <a href="/wiki/Diether_von_Isenburg" title="Diether von Isenburg">Diether von Isenburg</a>, who was elected Archbishop by the <a href="/wiki/Chapter_(religion)" title="Chapter (religion)">cathedral chapter</a> and supported by the citizens, and <a href="/wiki/Adolf_II_von_Nassau" class="mw-redirect" title="Adolf II von Nassau">Adolf II von Nassau</a>, who had been named archbishop for Mainz by the pope. In 1462, the Archbishop Adolf raided the city of Mainz, plundering and killing 400 inhabitants. At a tribunal, those who had survived lost all their property, which was then divided between those who promised to follow Adolf. Those who would not promise to follow Adolf (amongst them <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Gutenberg" title="Johannes Gutenberg">Johannes Gutenberg</a>) were driven out of the town or thrown into prison. The new archbishop revoked the city charter of Mainz and put the city under his direct rule. Ironically, after the death of Adolf II his successor was again Diether von Isenburg, now legally elected by the chapter and named by the Pope.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Jewish_community">Early Jewish community</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Early Jewish community">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Jewish community of Mainz dates to the 10th century CE. It is noted for its religious education. Rabbi <a href="/wiki/Gershom_ben_Judah" title="Gershom ben Judah">Gershom ben Judah</a> (960\xe2\x80\x931040) taught there, among others. He concentrated on the study of the <a href="/wiki/Talmud" title="Talmud">Talmud</a>, creating a German Jewish tradition. Mainz is also the legendary home of the martyred Rabbi <a href="/wiki/Amnon_of_Mainz" title="Amnon of Mainz">Amnon of Mainz</a>, composer of the <a href="/wiki/Unetanneh_Tokef" title="Unetanneh Tokef">Unetanneh Tokef</a> prayer. The Jews of Mainz, <a href="/wiki/Speyer" title="Speyer">Speyer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Worms,_Germany" title="Worms, Germany">Worms</a> created a supreme council to set standards in Jewish law and education in the 12th century.\n</p><p>The city of Mainz responded to the Jewish population in a variety of ways, behaving, in a sense, in a bipolar fashion towards them. Sometimes they were allowed freedom and were protected; at other times, they were persecuted. The Jews were expelled in 1012, 1462 (after which they were invited to return), and in 1474. Jews were attacked in <a href="/wiki/Rhineland_massacres" title="Rhineland massacres">1096</a> and by mobs in 1283. Outbreaks of the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> were usually blamed on the Jews, at which times they were massacred, such as the burning of 11 Jews alive in 1349.<sup id="cite_ref-Tuchman_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tuchman-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nowadays the Jewish community is growing rapidly, and a <a href="/wiki/New_synagogue_Mainz" class="mw-redirect" title="New synagogue Mainz">new synagogue</a> by the architect <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Herz" title="Manuel Herz">Manuel Herz</a> was constructed in 2010 on the site of the one destroyed by the Nazis on <i><a href="/wiki/Kristallnacht" title="Kristallnacht">Kristallnacht</a></i> in 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The community itself has 1,034 members, according to the <a href="/wiki/Central_Council_of_Jews_in_Germany" title="Central Council of Jews in Germany">Central Council of Jews in Germany</a>, and at least twice as many Jews altogether since many are unaffiliated with Judaism.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_Mainz">Republic of Mainz</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Republic of Mainz">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Mainz" title="Republic of Mainz">Republic of Mainz</a></div>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, the French Revolutionary army occupied Mainz in 1792; the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Mainz" class="mw-redirect" title="Archbishop of Mainz">Archbishop of Mainz</a>, Friedrich Karl Josef von Erthal, had already fled to <a href="/wiki/Aschaffenburg" title="Aschaffenburg">Aschaffenburg</a> by the time the French marched in. On 18 March 1793, the <a href="/wiki/Jacobin_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Jacobin Club">Jacobins</a> of Mainz, with other German democrats from about 130 towns in the <a href="/wiki/Palatinate_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Palatinate region">Rhenish Palatinate</a>, proclaimed the \'<a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Mainz" title="Republic of Mainz">Republic of Mainz</a>\'. Led by <a href="/wiki/Georg_Forster" title="Georg Forster">Georg Forster</a>, representatives of the Mainz Republic in Paris requested political affiliation of the Mainz Republic with France, but too late: <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a> was not entirely happy with the idea of a democratic free state on German soil (although the French dominated Mainz was neither free nor democratic). Prussian troops had already occupied the area and besieged Mainz by the end of March 1793. After a <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Mainz_(1793)" title="Siege of Mainz (1793)">siege</a> of 18 weeks, the French troops in Mainz surrendered on 23 July 1793; Prussians occupied the city and ended the Republic of Mainz. It came to the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mainz" title="Battle of Mainz">Battle of Mainz</a> in 1795 between Austria and France. Members of the Mainz <a href="/wiki/Jacobin_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Jacobin Club">Jacobin Club</a> were mistreated or imprisoned and punished for treason.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jeanbon2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Jeanbon2.jpg/220px-Jeanbon2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Jeanbon2.jpg/330px-Jeanbon2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Jeanbon2.jpg/440px-Jeanbon2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jeanbon2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tombstone of <a href="/wiki/Jean_Bon_Saint-Andr%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Jean Bon Saint-Andr\xc3\xa9">Jeanbon Baron de St. Andr\xc3\xa9</a>, Prefect of Napoleonic Mainz</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1797, the French returned. The army of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_I_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon I of France">Napol\xc3\xa9on Bonaparte</a> occupied the German territory to the west of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Campo_Formio" title="Treaty of Campo Formio">Treaty of Campo Formio</a> awarded France this entire area. On 17 February 1800, the French <i><a href="/wiki/Mont-Tonnerre" title="Mont-Tonnerre">D\xc3\xa9partement du Mont-Tonnerre</a></i> was founded here, with Mainz as its capital, the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> being the new eastern frontier of la Grande Nation. Austria and <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a> could not but approve this new border with France in 1801. However, after several defeats in Europe during the next years, the weakened Napol\xc3\xa9on and his troops had to leave Mainz in May 1814.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rhenish_Hesse">Rhenish Hesse</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Rhenish Hesse">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1816, the part of the former French D\xc3\xa9partement which is known today as <a href="/wiki/Rhenish_Hesse" title="Rhenish Hesse">Rhenish Hesse</a> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">Rheinhessen</i>) was awarded to the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Hesse" title="Grand Duchy of Hesse">Hesse-Darmstadt</a>, Mainz being the capital of the new <a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hessian</a> province of Rhenish Hesse. From 1816 to 1866, to the <a href="/wiki/German_Confederation" title="German Confederation">German Confederation</a> Mainz was the most important fortress in the defence against France, and had a strong garrison of Austrian, <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavarian</a> troops.\n</p><p>On the afternoon of 18 November 1857, a huge explosion rocked Mainz when the city\'s powder magazine, the <i>Pulverturm</i>, exploded. Approximately 150 people were killed and at least 500 injured; 57 buildings were destroyed and a similar number severely damaged in what was to be known as the <i>Powder Tower Explosion</i> or <i>Powder Explosion</i>.\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Prussian_War" title="Austro-Prussian War">Austro-Prussian War</a> in 1866, Mainz was declared a neutral zone. After the founding of the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> in 1871, Mainz no longer was as important a stronghold, because in the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">War of 1870/71</a> France had lost the territory of <a href="/wiki/Alsace-Lorraine" title="Alsace-Lorraine">Alsace-Lorraine</a> to Germany (which France had occupied bit by bit from 1630 to 1795), and this defined the new border between the two countries.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrial_expansion">Industrial expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Industrial expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainz_BlickzumRhein_1890.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Mainz_BlickzumRhein_1890.jpg/220px-Mainz_BlickzumRhein_1890.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Mainz_BlickzumRhein_1890.jpg/330px-Mainz_BlickzumRhein_1890.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Mainz_BlickzumRhein_1890.jpg/440px-Mainz_BlickzumRhein_1890.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3545" data-file-height="2597" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainz_BlickzumRhein_1890.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mainz towards the Rhine (around 1890)</div></div></div>\n<p>For centuries the inhabitants of the <a href="/wiki/Fortress_Mainz" class="mw-redirect" title="Fortress Mainz">fortress of Mainz</a> had suffered from a severe shortage of space which led to disease and other inconveniences. In 1872 Mayor <a href="/wiki/Carl_Wallau" title="Carl Wallau">Carl Wallau</a> and the council of Mainz persuaded the military government to sign a contract to expand the city. Beginning in 1874, the city of Mainz assimilated the <i>Gartenfeld</i>, an idyllic area of meadows and fields along the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> to the north of the rampart. The city expansion more than doubled the urban area which allowed Mainz to participate in the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrial revolution">industrial revolution</a> which had previously avoided the city for decades.\n</p><p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eduard_Krey%C3%9Fig&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eduard Krey\xc3\x9fig (page does not exist)">Eduard Krey\xc3\x9fig</a> was the man who made this happen. Having been the master builder of the city of Mainz since 1865, Krey\xc3\x9fig had the vision for the new part of town, the <i>Neustadt</i>. He also planned the first sewer system for the old part of town since Roman times and persuaded the city government to relocate the railway line from the Rhine side to the west end of the town. <a href="/wiki/Mainz_Hauptbahnhof" title="Mainz Hauptbahnhof">The main station</a> was built from 1882 to 1884 according to the plans of Philipp Johann Berdell\xc3\xa9.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainz-Stadtplan1898.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Mainz-Stadtplan1898.jpg/350px-Mainz-Stadtplan1898.jpg" decoding="async" width="350" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Mainz-Stadtplan1898.jpg/525px-Mainz-Stadtplan1898.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Mainz-Stadtplan1898.jpg/700px-Mainz-Stadtplan1898.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2812" data-file-height="1840" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainz-Stadtplan1898.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mainz including expansion zone the Rhine (1898)</div></div></div>\n<p>The Mainz master builder constructed a number of state-of-the-art public buildings, including the Mainz town hall \xe2\x80\x94 which was the largest of its kind in Germany at that time \xe2\x80\x94 as well a synagogue, the Rhine harbour and a number of public baths and school buildings. Krey\xc3\x9fig\'s last work was <a href="/wiki/Christuskirche,_Mainz" title="Christuskirche, Mainz">Christ Church</a> (<i>Christuskirche</i>), the largest Protestant church in the city and the first building constructed solely for the use of a Protestant congregation. In 1905 the demolition of the entire circumvallation and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rheingauwall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rheingauwall (page does not exist)">Rheingauwall</a> was taken in hand, according to imperial order of <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_II,_German_Emperor" title="Wilhelm II, German Emperor">Wilhelm II</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/German_Revolution_of_1918" class="mw-redirect" title="German Revolution of 1918">German Revolution of 1918</a> the <a href="/wiki/Mainz_Workers%27_and_Soldiers%27_Council" title="Mainz Workers&#39; and Soldiers&#39; Council">Mainz Workers\' and Soldiers\' Council</a> was formed which ran the city from 9 November until the arrival of French troops under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Rhineland" title="Occupation of the Rhineland">occupation of the Rhineland</a> agreed in the <a href="/wiki/Armistice" title="Armistice">Armistice</a>. The French occupation was confirmed by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> which went into effect 28 June 1919. The <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">Rhineland</a> (in which Mainz is located) was to be a demilitarized zone until 1935 and the French garrison, representing the <i><a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">Triple Entente</a></i>, was to stay until reparations were paid.\n</p><p>In 1923 Mainz participated in the Rhineland separatist movement that proclaimed a republic in the Rhineland. It collapsed in 1924. The French withdrew on 30 June 1930. <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> became chancellor of Germany in January 1933 and his political opponents, especially those of the Social Democratic Party, were either incarcerated or murdered. Some were able to move away from Mainz in time. One was the political organizer for the SPD, <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Kellner" title="Friedrich Kellner">Friedrich Kellner</a>, who went to Laubach, where as the chief justice inspector of the district court he continued his opposition against the Nazis by recording their misdeeds in a 900-page <a href="/wiki/My_Opposition" title="My Opposition">diary</a>.\n</p><p>In March 1933, a detachment from the <a href="/wiki/National_Socialist_German_Workers_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="National Socialist German Workers Party">National Socialist Party</a> in <a href="/wiki/Worms,_Germany" title="Worms, Germany">Worms</a> brought the party to Mainz. They hoisted the <a href="/wiki/Swastika" title="Swastika">swastika</a> on all public buildings and began to denounce the Jewish population in the newspapers. In 1936, the Nazis <a href="/wiki/Remilitarization_of_the_Rhineland" title="Remilitarization of the Rhineland">remilitarized the Rhineland</a> with great fanfare, the first move of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>\'s meteoric expansion. The former Triple Entente took no action.\n</p><p>During World War II the citadel at Mainz hosted the <a href="/wiki/Oflag_XII-B" title="Oflag XII-B">Oflag XII-B</a> prisoner of war camp.\n</p><p>The Bishop of Mainz, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Stohr" title="Albert Stohr">Albert Stohr</a>, formed an organization to help Jews escape from Germany.\n</p><p><span class="anchor" id="Allied_air_attacks"></span>During World War II, more than <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Mainz_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Mainz in World War II">30 air raids</a> destroyed about 80 percent of the city\'s center, including most of the historic buildings. Mainz was captured on 22 March 1945 against uneven German resistance (staunch in some sectors and weak in other parts of the city) by the <a href="/wiki/90th_Infantry_Division_(United_States)" title="90th Infantry Division (United States)">90th Infantry Division</a> under <a href="/wiki/William_A._McNulty" title="William A. McNulty">William A. McNulty</a>, a formation of the XII Corps under Third Army commanded by General <a href="/wiki/George_S._Patton" title="George S. Patton">George S. Patton</a>, Jr.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Patton used the ancient strategic gateway through <i>Germania Superior</i> to cross the Rhine south of Mainz, drive down the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> towards <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> and end the possibility of a Bavarian redoubt crossing the Alps in Austria when the war ended.\n</p><p>From 1945 to 1949, the city was part of the French zone of occupation. When the state of <a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a> was founded on 30 August 1946 by the commander of the French army on the French occupation zone <a href="/wiki/Marie_Pierre_K%C5%93nig" class="mw-redirect" title="Marie Pierre K\xc5\x93nig">Marie Pierre K\xc5\x93nig</a>, Mainz became capital of the new state.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> In 1962, the diarist, <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Kellner" title="Friedrich Kellner">Friedrich Kellner</a>, returned to spend his last years in Mainz. His life in Mainz, and the impact of his <a href="/wiki/My_Opposition" title="My Opposition">writings</a>, is the subject of the Canadian documentary <i><a href="/wiki/My_Opposition:_The_Diaries_of_Friedrich_Kellner" title="My Opposition: The Diaries of Friedrich Kellner">My Opposition: The Diaries of Friedrich Kellner</a></i>.\n</p><p>Following the withdrawal of French forces from Mainz, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Army Europe">United States Army Europe</a> occupied the military bases in Mainz. Today USAREUR only occupies McCulley Barracks in Wackernheim and the <a href="/wiki/Mainz_Sand_Dunes" title="Mainz Sand Dunes">Mainz Sand Dunes</a> for training area. Mainz is home to the headquarters of the <i>Bundeswehr\'</i>s <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Landeskommando&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Landeskommando (page does not exist)">Landeskommando</a></i> Rhineland-Palatinate and other units.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Minority_groups">Minority groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Mainz_May2007_cropped.jpg/700px-Mainz_May2007_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="700" height="154" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Mainz_May2007_cropped.jpg/1400px-Mainz_May2007_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="564" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div title="S\xc3\xbcdbr\xc3\xbccke, Mainz">South Railway bridge</a> over the Rhine looking north</div></div></div></div>\n<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:702px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainz_Panorama_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Mainz_Panorama_1.jpg/700px-Mainz_Panorama_1.jpg" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Mainz_Panorama_1.jpg/1400px-Mainz_Panorama_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="12632" data-file-height="1904" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainz_Panorama_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mainz May 2011, Schillerplatz, looking southeast</div></div></div></div>\n<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:702px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainz_Panorama_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Mainz_Panorama_2.jpg/700px-Mainz_Panorama_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="700" height="132" class="thumbimage" class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainz_Panorama_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Schusterstra\xc3\x9fe</div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The destruction caused by the <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bombing_during_World_War_II" title="Strategic bombing during World War II">bombing of Mainz during World War II</a> led to the most intense phase of building in the history of the town. During the last war in Germany, more than 30 air raids destroyed about 80 percent of the city\'s center, including most of the historic buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The destructive attack on the afternoon of 27 February 1945 remains the most destructive of all 33 bombings that Mainz has suffered in World War II in the collective memory of most of the population living then. The air raid caused most of the dead and made an already hard-hit city largely leveled.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rathaus_Mainz_Jockel-Fuchs-Platz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Rathaus_Mainz_Jockel-Fuchs-Platz.jpg/220px-Rathaus_Mainz_Jockel-Fuchs-Platz.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="71" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Rathaus_Mainz_Jockel-Fuchs-Platz.jpg/330px-Rathaus_Mainz_Jockel-Fuchs-Platz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Rathaus_Mainz_Jockel-Fuchs-Platz.jpg/440px-Rathaus_Mainz_Jockel-Fuchs-Platz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="9204" data-file-height="2960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rathaus_Mainz_Jockel-Fuchs-Platz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Town Hall by Jacobsen</div></div></div>\n<p>Nevertheless, the post-war reconstruction took place very slowly. While cities such as Frankfurt had been rebuilt fast by a central authority, only individual efforts were initially successful in rebuilding Mainz. The reason for this was that the French wanted Mainz to expand and to become a model city. Mainz lay within the <a href="/wiki/Allied-occupied_Germany" title="Allied-occupied Germany">French-controlled sector of Germany</a> and it was a French architect and town-planner, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Marcel_Lods&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Marcel Lods (page does not exist)">Marcel Lods</a>, who produced a Le Corbusier-style plan of an ideal architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> But the very first interest of the inhabitants was the restoration of housing areas. Even after the failure of the model city plans it was the initiative of the French (founding of the Johannes Gutenberg <a href="/wiki/University_of_Mainz" title="University of Mainz">University of Mainz</a>, elevation of Mainz to the state capital of Rhineland-Palatinate, the early resumption of the <a href="/wiki/Mainz_carnival" title="Mainz carnival">Mainz carnival</a>) driving the city in a positive development after the war. The City Plan of 1958 by <a href="/wiki/Ernst_May" title="Ernst May">Ernst May</a> allowed a regulated reconstruction for the first time. In 1950, the seat of the government of Rhineland-Palatinate had been transferred to the new Mainz and in 1963 the seat of the new ZDF, notable architects were Adolf Bayer, Richard J\xc3\xb6rg and Egon Hartmann. At the time of the two-thousand-years-anniversary in 1962 the city was largely reconstructed. During the 1950s and 1960s the Oberstadt had been extended, M\xc3\xbcnchfeld and Lerchenberg added as suburbs, the Altstadttangente (<a href="/wiki/Automobile_dependency" title="Automobile dependency">intersection of the old town</a>), new <a href="/wiki/Neighbourhood" title="Neighbourhood">neighbourhoods</a> as Westring and S\xc3\xbcdring contributed to the extension. By 1970 there remained only a few ruins. The new town hall of Mainz had been designed by <a href="/wiki/Arne_Jacobsen" title="Arne Jacobsen">Arne Jacobsen</a> and finished by <a href="/wiki/Dissing%2BWeitling" title="Dissing+Weitling">Dissing+Weitling</a>. The town used Jacobsens activity for the Danish <a href="/wiki/Novo_Nordisk" title="Novo Nordisk">Novo</a> erecting a new office and warehouse building to contact him. The <a href="/wiki/Urban_renewal" title="Urban renewal">urban renewal</a> of the old town changed the inner city. In the framework of the preparation of the cathedrals millennium, <a href="/wiki/Pedestrian_zone" title="Pedestrian zone">pedestrian zones</a> were developed around the cathedral, in northern direction to the Neubrunnenplatz and in southern direction across the Leichhof to the Augustinerstra\xc3\x9fe and Kirschgarten. The 1980s brought the renewal of the fa\xc3\xa7ades on the Markt and a new inner-city neighbourhood on the K\xc3\xa4strich. During the 1990s the Kisselberg between Gonsenheim and Bretzenheim, the "Fort Malakoff Center" at the site of the old police barracks, the renewal of the Main Station and the demolition of the first post-war shopping center at the Markt followed by the erection of a new historicising building at the same place.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">Main sights</span><span
