synagogue in Mainz</a></li>\n<li>Kunsthalle Mainz \xe2\x80\x93 museum for contemporary art</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Humbrechthof" title="Humbrechthof">Humbrechthof</a>, later called Sch\xc3\xb6fferhof, the building in which Johannes Gutenberg developed his technique of printing</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The city of Mainz is divided into 15 local districts according to the main statute of the city of Mainz. Each local district has a district administration of 13 members and a directly elected mayor, who is the chairman of the district administration. This local council decides on important issues affecting the local area, however, the final decision on new policies is made by the Mainz\'s municipal council.\n</p><p>In accordance with section 29 paragraph 2 Local Government Act of <a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a>, which refers to municipalities of more than 150,000 inhabitants, the city council has 60 members.\n</p><p>Districts of the town are:\n</p>\n<table cellpadding="20">\n\n<tbody><tr valign="top">\n<td>\n<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Altstadt_(Mainz)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Altstadt (Mainz) (page does not exist)">Altstadt</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bretzenheim_(Mainz)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bretzenheim (Mainz) (page does not exist)">Bretzenheim</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Drais" title="Drais">Drais</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ebersheim_(Mainz)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ebersheim (Mainz) (page does not exist)">Ebersheim</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Finthen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Finthen (page does not exist)">Finthen</a></li></ul>\n</td>\n<td>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Gonsenheim" title="Gonsenheim">Gonsenheim</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hartenberg-M%C3%BCnchfeld" title="Hartenberg-M\xc3\xbcnchfeld">Hartenberg-M\xc3\xbcnchfeld</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Hechtsheim&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hechtsheim (page does not exist)">Hechtsheim</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Laubenheim_(Mainz)" class="mw-redirect" title="Laubenheim (Mainz)">Laubenheim</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mainz-Lerchenberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Mainz-Lerchenberg">Lerchenberg</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mainz-Lerchenberg" class="extiw" title="de:Mainz-Lerchenberg">de</a>&#93;</span></li></ul>\n</td>\n<td>\n<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marienborn_(Mainz)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Marienborn (Mainz) (page does not exist)">Marienborn</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mombach" title="Mombach">Mombach</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Neustadt(Mainz)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Neustadt(Mainz) (page does not exist)">Neustadt</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Oberstadt(Mainz)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Oberstadt(Mainz) (page does not exist)">Oberstadt</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Weisenau&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Weisenau (page does not exist)">Weisenau</a></li></ul>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Until 1945, the districts of <a href="/wiki/Bischofsheim_(Mainspitze)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bischofsheim (Mainspitze)">Bischofsheim</a> (now an independent town), <a href="/wiki/Ginsheim-Gustavsburg" title="Ginsheim-Gustavsburg">Ginsheim-Gustavsburg</a> (which together are an independent town) belonged to Mainz. The former districts <a href="/wiki/Mainz-Am%C3%B6neburg" title="Mainz-Am\xc3\xb6neburg">Am\xc3\xb6neburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mainz-Kastel" title="Mainz-Kastel">Kastel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mainz-Kostheim" title="Mainz-Kostheim">Kostheim</a> \xe2\x80\x94 (in short, <i>AKK</i>) are now administrated by the city of <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden" title="Wiesbaden">Wiesbaden</a> (on the north bank of the river). The AKK was separated from Mainz when the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> was designated the boundary between the French occupation zone (the later state of <a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a>) and the U.S. occupation zone (<a href="/wiki/Hesse" title="Hesse">Hesse</a>) in 1945.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Coat of arms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wheel_of_Mainz" title="Wheel of Mainz">Wheel of Mainz</a></div>\n<p>The coat of arms of Mainz is derived from the coat of arms of the <a href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Mainz" class="mw-redirect" title="Archbishopric of Mainz">Archbishops of Mainz</a> and features two six-spoked silver wheels connected by a silver cross on a red background.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainz-flags.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Mainz-flags.jpg/220px-Mainz-flags.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Mainz-flags.jpg/330px-Mainz-flags.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Mainz-flags.jpg/440px-Mainz-flags.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainz-flags.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mainz Rad and FSV Mainz 05 flags on the Domplatz</div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Mainz is home to a <a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">Carnival</a>, the <i>Mainzer Fassenacht</i> or <i>Fastnacht</i>, which has developed since the early 19th century. Carnival in Mainz has its roots in the criticism of social and political injustices under the shelter of cap and bells. Today, the uniforms of many traditional Carnival clubs still imitate and caricature the uniforms of the French and Prussian troops of the past. The height of the carnival season is on <a href="/wiki/Rosenmontag" title="Rosenmontag">Rosenmontag</a> ("rose Monday"), when there is a large parade in Mainz, with more than 500,000 people celebrating in the streets.\n</p><p>The first ever <a href="/wiki/Katholikentag" title="Katholikentag">Katholikentag</a>, a festival-like gathering of German Catholics, was held in Mainz in 1848.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Uni-Mainz-Forum-Januar_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Uni-Mainz-Forum-Januar_2006.jpg/220px-Uni-Mainz-Forum-Januar_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Uni-Mainz-Forum-Januar_2006.jpg/330px-Uni-Mainz-Forum-Januar_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Uni-Mainz-Forum-Januar_2006.jpg/440px-Uni-Mainz-Forum-Januar_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Uni-Mainz-Forum-Januar_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Forum of the <i>Johannes Gutenberg University</i> of Mainz</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Johannes_Gutenberg" title="Johannes Gutenberg">Johannes Gutenberg</a>, credited with the invention of the modern <a href="/wiki/Printing_press" title="Printing press">printing press</a> with movable type, was born here and died here. Since 1968 the <a href="/wiki/Johannisnacht,_Mainz" title="Johannisnacht, Mainz">Mainzer Johannisnacht</a> commemorates the person Johannes Gutenberg in his native city. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Mainz" title="University of Mainz">Mainz University</a>, which was refounded in 1946, is named after <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Gutenberg" title="Johannes Gutenberg">Gutenberg</a>; the earlier University of Mainz that dated back to 1477 had been closed down by Napoleon\'s troops in 1798.\n</p><p>Mainz was one of three important centers of <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> theology and learning in Central Europe during the Middle Ages. Known collectively as <i>Shum</i>, the cities of <a href="/wiki/Speyer" title="Speyer">Speyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Worms,_Germany" title="Worms, Germany">Worms</a> and Mainz played a key role in the preservation and propagation of Talmudic scholarship.\n</p><p>The city is the seat of Zweites Deutsches Fernsehen (literally, "Second German Television", <a href="/wiki/ZDF" title="ZDF">ZDF</a>), one of two federal nationwide TV broadcasters. There are also a couple of radio stations based in Mainz.\n</p><p>Other cultural aspects of the city include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>As city in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Region">Greater Region</a>, Mainz participated in the program of the year of <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> 2007.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Walk_of_Fame_of_Cabaret" title="Walk of Fame of Cabaret">Walk of Fame of Cabaret</a> may be found nearby the Schillerplatz.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Music_publisher_(popular_music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Music publisher (popular music)">music publisher</a> <a href="/wiki/Schott_Music" title="Schott Music">Schott Music</a> is located in Mainz.</li>\n<li>One of the oldest brass instrument manufacturers in the world, <a href="/wiki/Gebr._Alexander" class="mw-redirect" title="Gebr. Alexander">Gebr. Alexander</a> is located in Mainz.</li>\n<li>Fans of Gospel music enjoy the yearly performances of <a href="/wiki/Colours_of_Gospel" title="Colours of Gospel">Colours of Gospel</a>.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Mainz" title="University of Mainz">University of Mainz</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Applied_Sciences_Mainz" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Applied Sciences Mainz">University of Applied Sciences Mainz</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Catholic_University_of_Applied_Sciences_Mainz" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic University of Applied Sciences Mainz">Catholic University of Applied Sciences Mainz</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coface-Arena_(8208664309).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Coface-Arena_%288208664309%29.jpg/220px-Coface-Arena_%288208664309%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Coface-Arena_%288208664309%29.jpg/330px-Coface-Arena_%288208664309%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Coface-Arena_%288208664309%29.jpg/440px-Coface-Arena_%288208664309%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1126" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coface-Arena_(8208664309).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Opel_Arena_(stadium)" title="Opel Arena (stadium)">Opel Arena</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The local football club <a href="/wiki/1._FSV_Mainz_05" title="1. FSV Mainz 05">1. FSV Mainz 05</a> has a long history in the German football leagues. Since 2004 it has competed in the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> (First German soccer league) except a break in second level in 2007\xe2\x80\x9308 season. Mainz is closely associated with renowned coach <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Klopp" title="J\xc3\xbcrgen Klopp">J\xc3\xbcrgen Klopp</a>, who spent the vast majority of his playing career at the club and was also the manager for seven years, leading the club to Bundesliga football for the first time. After leaving Mainz Klopp went on to win two Bundesliga titles and reaching a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> final with <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a>. In the summer 2011 the club opened its new stadium called <a href="/wiki/Coface_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Coface Arena">Coface Arena</a>, which was later renamed to Opel Arena. Further relevant football clubs are <a href="/wiki/TSV_Schott_Mainz" title="TSV Schott Mainz">TSV Schott Mainz</a>, <a href="/wiki/SV_Gonsenheim" title="SV Gonsenheim">SV Gonsenheim</a>, Fontana Finthen, FC Fortuna Mombach and FVgg Mombach 03.\n</p><p>The local wrestling club ASV Mainz 1888 is currently in the top division of team wrestling in Germany, the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga_(wrestling)" title="Bundesliga (wrestling)">Bundesliga</a>. In 1973, 1977 and 2012 the ASV Mainz 1888 won the German championship.\n</p><p>In 2007 the <a href="/wiki/Mainz_Athletics" title="Mainz Athletics">Mainz Athletics</a> won the <a href="/wiki/German_champions_(baseball)#German_Men&#39;s_Champions" title="German champions (baseball)">German Men\'s Championship in baseball</a>.\n</p><p>As a result of the 2008 invasion of Georgia by Russian troops, Mainz acted as a neutral venue for the Georgian Vs Republic of Ireland football game.\n</p><p>The biggest basketball club in the city is the ASC Theresianum Mainz. Its men\'s team is playing in the Regionalliga and its women\'s team is playing in the 2.DBBL.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="USC_Mainz">USC Mainz</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: USC Mainz">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><b>Universit\xc3\xa4ts-Sportclub Mainz</b> (University Sports Club Mainz) is a German sports club based in Mainz. It was founded on 9 September 1959<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> by Berno Wischmann primarily for students of the University of Mainz. It is considered one of the most powerful Athletics Sports clubs in Germany. 50 athletes of USC have distinguished themselves in a half-century in club history at Olympic Games, World and European Championships. In particular in the decathlon dominated USC athletes for decades: Already at the European Championships in Budapest in 1966 Mainz won three (Werner von Moltke, J\xc3\xb6rg Mattheis and Horst Beyer) all decathlon medals. In the all-time list of the USC, there are nine athletes who have achieved more than 8,000 points \xe2\x80\x93 at the head of Siegfried Wentz (8762 points in 1983) and Guido Kratschmer (1980 world record with 8667 points). Most successful athlete of the association is more fighter, sprinter and long jumper Ingrid Becker (Olympic champion in 1968 in the pentathlon and Olympic champion in 1972 in the 4 \xc3\x97 100 Metres Relay and European champion in 1971 in the long jump). Most famous athletes of the present are the sprinter Marion Wagner (world champion in 2001 in the 4 \xc3\x97 100 Metres Relay) and the pole vaulters Carolin Hingst (Eighth of the 2008 Olympics in Beijing) and Anna Battke.\n</p><p>Three world titles adorn the balance of USC Mainz. For the discus thrower Lars Riedel attended (1991 and 1993) and the already mentioned sprinter Marion Wagner (2001). Added to 5 titles at the European Championships, a total of 65 international medals and 260 victories at the German Athletics Championships.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The players of USC\'s basketball section played from the season 1968/69 to the season 1974/75 in the National Basketball League (BBL) of the German Basketball Federation (DBB). As a finalist to winning the DBB Cup in 1971 USC Mainz played in the <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_FIBA_European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="1971\xe2\x80\x9372 FIBA European Cup Winners&#39; Cup">1971\xe2\x80\x9372 FIBA European Cup Winners\' Cup</a> against the Italian Cup winners of <a href="/wiki/Fides_Napoli" class="mw-redirect" title="Fides Napoli">Fides Napoli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mainz_Athletics">Mainz Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Mainz Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mainz_Athletics" title="Mainz Athletics">Mainz Athletics</a></div>\n<p>The <b>Baseball and Softball Club Mainz Athletics</b>  is a German baseball and softball club located in the city of Mainz in <a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a>. The Athletics is one of the largest clubs in the <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga_(baseball)" title="Bundesliga (baseball)">Baseball-Bundesliga S\xc3\xbcd</a> in terms of membership, claiming to have hundreds of active players. The club has played in the Baseball-Bundesliga for more than two decades, and has won the German Championship in 2007 and 2016.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mz-bonifaziustuerme.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Mz-bonifaziustuerme.jpg/220px-Mz-bonifaziustuerme.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Mz-bonifaziustuerme.jpg/330px-Mz-bonifaziustuerme.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Mz-bonifaziustuerme.jpg/440px-Mz-bonifaziustuerme.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mz-bonifaziustuerme.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonifatius center building</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wine_centre">Wine centre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Wine centre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Mainz has been a wine-growing region since Roman times and is one of the centers of the <a href="/wiki/German_wine" title="German wine">German wine</a> industry.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Since 2008, the city is a member of the Great Wine Capitals Global Network (GWC), an association of well-known wineculture-cities of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\nMany wine traders work in the city. The <a href="/wiki/Sparkling_wine" title="Sparkling wine">sparkling wine</a> producer Kupferberg produced in Mainz-Hechtsheim and <a href="/wiki/Henkell" class="mw-redirect" title="Henkell">Henkell</a> \xe2\x80\x94 now located on the other side of the river Rhine \xe2\x80\x94 were once founded in Mainz. The famous <a href="/wiki/Blue_Nun" title="Blue Nun">Blue Nun</a>, one of the first branded wines, was marketed by the Sichel family. The <i>Haus des Deutschen Weines</i> (English: House of German Wine), is located in the city. The Mainzer Weinmarkt (wine market) is one of the great wine fairs in Germany.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_industries">Other industries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Other industries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Schott_AG" title="Schott AG">Schott AG</a>, one of the world\'s largest glass manufactures, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Werner_%26_Mertz" title="Werner &amp; Mertz">Werner &amp; Mertz</a>, a large chemical factory, are based in Mainz. Other companies such as <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, <a href="/wiki/QUINN_group#QUINN_Plastics" class="mw-redirect" title="QUINN group">QUINN Plastics</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Novo_Nordisk" title="Novo Nordisk">Novo Nordisk</a> have their German administration in Mainz as well.  <a href="/wiki/BioNTech" title="BioNTech">BioNTech</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> company developing <a href="/wiki/Immunotherapy" title="Immunotherapy">immunotherapies</a> including a promising candidate vaccine against <a href="/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019" class="mw-redirect" title="Coronavirus disease 2019">coronavirus disease 2019</a> (COVID\xe2\x80\x9119) was founded in 2008 in Mainz by Turkish-German scientists <a href="/wiki/U%C4%9Fur_%C5%9Eahin" title="U\xc4\x9fur \xc5\x9eahin">U\xc4\x9fur \xc5\x9eahin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/%C3%96zlem_T%C3%BCreci" title="\xc3\x96zlem T\xc3\xbcreci">\xc3\x96zlem T\xc3\xbcreci</a>, with the Austrian oncologist Christoph Huber.  \n</p><p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Johann-Joseph_Krug&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Johann-Joseph Krug (page does not exist)">Johann-Joseph Krug</a>, founder of France\'s famous <a href="/wiki/Champagne_Krug" title="Champagne Krug">Krug</a> champagne house in 1843, was born in Mainz in 1800.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:802px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Blick-auf-mainz-aus-richtung-der-schiersteiner-bruecke.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Blick-auf-mainz-aus-richtung-der-schiersteiner-bruecke.jpg/800px-Blick-auf-mainz-aus-richtung-der-schiersteiner-bruecke.jpg" decoding="async" width="800" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Blick-auf-mainz-aus-richtung-der-schiersteiner-bruecke.jpg/1200px-Blick-auf-mainz-aus-richtung-der-schiersteiner-bruecke.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Blick-auf-mainz-aus-richtung-der-schiersteiner-bruecke.jpg/1600px-Blick-auf-mainz-aus-richtung-der-schiersteiner-bruecke.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10186" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Blick-auf-mainz-aus-richtung-der-schiersteiner-bruecke.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View to the Rheinreede, container cranes 2007, laid down in 2010.</div></div></div></div>\n<p>Mainz is a major transport hub in southern Germany. It is an important component in European distribution, as it has the fifth largest inter-modal port in Germany. The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Mainz" title="Port of Mainz">Port of Mainz</a>, now handling mainly containers, is a sizable industrial area to the north of the city, along the banks of the Rhine. In order to open up space along the city\'s riverfront for residential development, it was shifted further northwards in 2010.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainz_-_Luftaufnahme.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Mainz_-_Luftaufnahme.jpg/230px-Mainz_-_Luftaufnahme.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Mainz_-_Luftaufnahme.jpg/345px-Mainz_-_Luftaufnahme.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Mainz_-_Luftaufnahme.jpg/460px-Mainz_-_Luftaufnahme.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3330" data-file-height="2498" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mainz_-_Luftaufnahme.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial photograph of Mainz</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Mainz_Central_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Mainz Central Station">Mainz Central Station</a> or <i>Mainz Hauptbahnhof</i>, is frequented by 80,000 travelers and visitors each day and is therefore one of the busiest 21 stations in Germany. It is a stop for the <a href="/wiki/S-Bahn_Rhein-Main" class="mw-redirect" title="S-Bahn Rhein-Main">S-Bahn</a> line <a href="/wiki/S8_(Rhine-Main_S-Bahn)" title="S8 (Rhine-Main S-Bahn)">S8</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Rhein-Main-Verkehrsverbund" title="Rhein-Main-Verkehrsverbund">Rhein-Main-Verkehrsverbund</a>. Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/Mainbahn" class="mw-redirect" title="Mainbahn">Mainbahn</a> line to <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_(Main)_Hauptbahnhof" title="Frankfurt (Main) Hauptbahnhof">Frankfurt Hbf</a> starts at the station. It is served by 440 daily local and regional trains (<a href="/wiki/StadtExpress" class="mw-redirect" title="StadtExpress">StadtExpress</a>, <a href="/wiki/RegionalExpress" class="mw-redirect" title="RegionalExpress">RE</a> and <a href="/wiki/Regionalbahn" title="Regionalbahn">RB</a>) and 78 long-distance trains (<a href="/wiki/InterCity" title="InterCity">IC</a>, <a href="/wiki/EuroCity" title="EuroCity">EC</a> and <a href="/wiki/InterCityExpress" class="mw-redirect" title="InterCityExpress">ICE</a>). Intercity-Express lines connect Mainz with Frankfurt (Main), <a href="/wiki/Karlsruhe_Hbf" class="mw-redirect" title="Karlsruhe Hbf">Karlsruhe Hbf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Worms_Hauptbahnhof" title="Worms Hauptbahnhof">Worms Hauptbahnhof</a> and <a href="/wiki/Koblenz_Hauptbahnhof" title="Koblenz Hauptbahnhof">Koblenz Hauptbahnhof</a>. It is a terminus of the <a href="/wiki/West_Rhine_Railway" title="West Rhine Railway">West Rhine Railway</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mainz%E2%80%93Ludwigshafen_railway" title="Mainz\xe2\x80\x93Ludwigshafen railway">Mainz\xe2\x80\x93Ludwigshafen railway</a>, as well as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alzey%E2%80%93Mainz_Railway&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alzey\xe2\x80\x93Mainz Railway (page does not exist)">Alzey\xe2\x80\x93Mainz Railway</a> erected by the <a href="/wiki/Hessische_Ludwigsbahn" class="mw-redirect" title="Hessische Ludwigsbahn">Hessische Ludwigsbahn</a> in 1871. Access to the <a href="/wiki/East_Rhine_Railway" title="East Rhine Railway">East Rhine Railway</a> is provided by the <a href="/wiki/Kaiserbr%C3%BCcke_(Mainz)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaiserbr\xc3\xbccke (Mainz)">Kaiserbr\xc3\xbccke</a>, a railway bridge across the Rhine at the north end of Mainz.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Operational_usage">Operational usage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Operational usage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<table border="0" cellpadding="2" cellspacing="2" style="float:left; margin-right:1em; background:#f3f3f3;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="2">In brief\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:#fff;">\n<td>Number of passenger tracks<br />above ground:\n</td>\n<td>7 <a href="/wiki/Rail_terminology#M" class="mw-redirect" title="Rail terminology">main line</a>,<br />1 branch,<br />1 <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tramway</a> station,<br /> 2 tracks each\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="background:#fff;">\n<td>Trains<br />(daily):\n</td>\n<td>78 long-distance<br />440 regional<br />\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transportation">Public transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Public transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The station is an interchange point for the <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Mainz" title="Trams in Mainz">Mainz tramway network</a>, and an important bus junction for the city and region (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Rhein-Nahe-Nahverkehrsverbund&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rhein-Nahe-Nahverkehrsverbund (page does not exist)">RNN</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Omnibusverkehr_Rhein-Nahe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Omnibusverkehr Rhein-Nahe (page does not exist)">ORN</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainzer_Verkehrsgesellschaft&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mainzer Verkehrsgesellschaft (page does not exist)">MVG</a>).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cycling">Cycling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Cycling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Mainz offers a wide array of bicycle transportation facilities and events, including several miles of on-street bike lanes. The <a href="/wiki/EV15_The_Rhine_Cycle_Route" title="EV15 The Rhine Cycle Route">Rheinradweg</a> (Rhine Cycle Route) is an international cycle route, running from the source to the mouth of the Rhine, traversing four countries at a distance of 1,300&#160;km (810&#160;mi). Another cycling tour runs towards Bingen and further to the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Rhine" title="Middle Rhine">Middle Rhine</a>, a <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Europe">UNESCO World Heritage Site (2002)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_transportation">Air transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Air transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Mainz is served by <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a>, the busiest airport by passenger traffic in Germany by far, the third busiest in Europe and the ninth busiest worldwide in 2009. Located about 10 miles (16 kilometres) east of Mainz, it is connected to the city by an <a href="/wiki/S8_(Rhine-Main_S-Bahn)" title="S8 (Rhine-Main S-Bahn)">S-Bahn line</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-air_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-air-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The small <a href="/wiki/Mainz_Finthen_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Mainz Finthen Airport">Mainz Finthen Airport</a>, located just 3 miles (5&#160;km) southwest of Mainz, is used by <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a> only. Another airport, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt-Hahn_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt-Hahn Airport">Frankfurt-Hahn Airport</a> located about 50 miles (80&#160;km) west of Mainz, is served by a few <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost carriers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-air_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-air-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_people_related_to_Mainz" class="mw-redirect" title="List of people related to Mainz">List of people related to Mainz</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Electorate_of_Mainz" title="Electorate of Mainz">Archbishops of Mainz</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Mainz" title="List of mayors of Mainz">List of mayors of Mainz</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_\xe2\x80\x93_sister_cities">Twin towns \xe2\x80\x93 sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Twin towns \xe2\x80\x93 sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div title="Baku">Baku</a>, Azerbaijan (1984)</li></ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_names">Alternative names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Alternative names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Mainz has a number of <a href="/wiki/Names_of_European_cities_in_different_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Names of European cities in different languages">different names</a> in other languages and dialects. In <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> it is known as <i><i lang="la" title="Latin-language text">Mogontiacum</i></i> or <i><i lang="la" title="Latin-language text">Moguntiacum</i></i> and, in the local <a href="/wiki/West_Middle_German" class="mw-redirect" title="West Middle German">West Middle German</a> dialect, it is <i>M\xc3\xa4\xc3\xa4nz</i> or <i>Meenz</i>. It is known as <i><i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Mayence</i></i> in French, <i><i lang="it" title="Italian-language text">Magonza</i></i> in Italian, <i><i lang="es" title="Spanish-language text">Maguncia</i></i> in Spanish, <i><i lang="pt" title="Portuguese-language text">Mog\xc3\xbancia</i></i> in Portuguese, <i><i lang="pl" title="Polish-language text">Moguncja</i></i> in Polish, <i>Magentza</i> (<span lang="yi" dir="rtl" title="Yiddish-language text">\xd7\x9e\xd7\x92\xd7\xa0\xd7\xa6\xd7\x90</span>) in Yiddish, and <i><i lang="cs" title="Czech-language text">Mohu\xc4\x8d</i></i> in Czech and Slovakian.\n</p><p>Before the 20th century, Mainz was commonly known in English as <i>Mentz</i> or by its French name of <i>Mayence</i>. It is the namesake of two American cities named <a href="/wiki/Mentz_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Mentz (disambiguation)">Mentz</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mainz&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: See Retrieved <span class="nowrap">11 June</span> 2014</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Einwohner_nach_Stadtteilen&amp;rft.au=Landeshauptstadt+Mainz&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fmainz.de%2FC1256D6E003D3E93%2FvwLookupImagesforLoad%2Feinwohner-stadtteile-2013-12-31.pdf%2F%24FILE%2Feinwohner-stadtteile-2013-12-31.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMainz" class="Z3988"></span></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Olaf H\xc3\xb6ckmann: <i>Mainz als r\xc3\xb6mische Hafenstadt</i>. p.&#160;87\xe2\x80\x93106. in: Michael J. Klein (editor): <i>Die R\xc3\xb6mer und ihr Erbe. Fortschritt durch Innovation und Integration</i>. Philipp von Zabern, Mainz 2003, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3-8053-2948-2" title="Special:BookSources/3-8053-2948-2">3-8053-2948-2</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.intellicast.com/Local/History.aspx?location=GMXX0080">"Mainz historic weather averages"</a>. Intellicast. June 2011<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">21 September</span> 2009</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Mainz+historic+weather+averages&amp;rft.pub=Intellicast&amp;rft.date=2011-06&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.intellicast.com%2FLocal%2FHistory.aspx%3Flocation%3DGMXX0080&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMainz" class="Z3988"></span></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The earliest certain evidence of the existence of <i>Mogontiacum</i> is the account of the death and funeral of <a href="/wiki/Nero_Claudius_Drusus" title="Nero Claudius Drusus">Nero Claudius Drusus</a>, brother of the future emperor, <a href="/wiki/Tiberius" title="Tiberius">Tiberius</a>, given in <a href="/wiki/Suetonius" title="Suetonius">Suetonius</a>\' life of Drusus. Few leaders have been as loved and as popular as Drusus. He fell from his horse in 9 BC, contracted gangrene and lingered several days. His brother Tiberius reached him in just a few days riding post-horses over the Roman roads and served as the chief mourner, walking with the deceased in a funeral procession from the summer camp where he had fallen to Mogontiacum, where the soldiers insisted on a funeral. The body was transported to Rome, cremated in the Campus Martis and the ashes placed in the tomb of <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a>, who was still alive, and wrote poetry and delivered a state funeral oration for him. If Drusus founded Mogontiacum the earliest date is the start of his campaign, 13 BC. Some hypothesize that Mogontiacum was constructed at one of two earlier opportunities, one when <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Agrippa" class="mw-redirect" title="Marcus Agrippa">Marcus Agrippa</a> campaigned in the region in 42 BC or by <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a> himself after 58 BC. Lack of evidence plays a part in favoring 13 BC. No sources cite Mogontiacum before 13 BC, no legions are known to have been stationed there, and no coins survive.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Inline_citation#When_you_must_use_inline_citations" title="Wikipedia:Inline citation"><span title="The text near this tag needs a citation. (August 2010)">This quote needs a citation</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite id="CITEREFvon_Elbe1975" class="citation book cs1">von Elbe, Joachim (1975). <i>Roman Germany: a guide to sites and museums</i>. Mainz: P. von Zabern. p.&#160;253.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Roman+Germany%3A+a+guide+to+sites+and+museums&amp;rft.place=Mainz&amp;rft.pages=253&amp;rft.pub=P.+von+Zabern&amp;rft.date=1975&amp;rft.aulast=von+Elbe&amp;rft.aufirst=Joachim&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMainz" class="Z3988"></span></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A second hypothesis suggests that Moguns was a wealthy Celt whose estate was taken for the fort and that a tax district was formed on the area parallel to other tax districts with a -iacum suffix (Arenacum, Mannaricium). There is no evidence for this supposedly wealthy man or his estate, but there is plenty for the god. According to <a href="/wiki/Carl_Darling_Buck" title="Carl Darling Buck">Carl Darling Buck</a> in <i>Comparative Grammar of Greek and Latin</i>, -yo- and -k- are general Indo-European formative suffices and are not related to taxes. As the loyalty of the <a href="/wiki/Vangiones" title="Vangiones">Vangiones</a> was unquestioned and Drusus was campaigning over the Rhine, it is unlikely Mogontiacum would have been built to collect taxes from the Vangiones, who were not a Roman <i>municipium</i>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text"
